Liaoning Province Implements Abolishing Likin 71

The Finance Department Orders All Tax Bureaus to Stop Collecting Taxes Immediately

Shenyang correspondence. All likin taxes in all provinces of the country, and all donations and taxes similar to likin, have been explicitly ordered by the central government to be abolished from January 1. Although the northeastern provinces have never had likin or other names, there are quite a few donations and taxes similar to likin. In order to obey the explicit order of the central government and relieve the suffering of the people, Deputy Commander Zhang has telegraphed the northeastern provinces a few days ago to follow the instructions. The Finance Department of Liaoning Province has repeatedly considered this case.

The sales tax levied in the northeastern provinces has a huge annual income, and military and political expenses rely on it. Once it is abolished, the loss to the provincial treasury will be not small. Director Zhang Zhenlu and the chairman of the provincial government, Zang Shiyi, have seriously studied it, and they should ask for a postponement due to the special circumstances of the eastern provinces. Later, Zhang's vice-commander replied by telegram, urging immediate implementation to show his sincerity in supporting the central government, and ordering the establishment of business tax and special consumption tax to compensate for the losses. After receiving the order, Director Zhang immediately convened a meeting of the section chiefs, secretaries, and directors of the three bureaus in the provincial capital to discuss the results. They all agreed that although the current sales tax in the province is the business tax promulgated by the central government, and the special consumption tax is the current production tax in the province, the collection methods and tax rates are different. We should follow the business tax and special consumption tax promulgated by the central government, and refer to the situation in our province to formulate the interim regulations and collection rules for each tax, and submit them to the provincial government for approval and promulgation. At the same time, on the 13th, a substitute telegram was issued, ordering all tax bureaus to immediately stop collecting taxes from the date of the order. Director Zhang of the Finance Department also took a special train to Tianjin at 9:00 AM on the 12th to pay respects to Vice Commander Zhang and Minister of Finance Song to discuss all financial matters in the Northeast. It is said that he will return to Shenyang in one or two days. (January 13)

The Plague in Haining is Rampant 72

Hangzhou correspondence. Since the beginning of winter, Haining has discovered an epidemic, which has become more rampant in recent days. More than ten people die every day. The original doctors are not enough to be distributed. Although the provincial authorities have sent doctors from the provincial infectious disease hospital and the municipal hospital to assist, the funding is very difficult. Now Haining's public groups have specially recommended Pang Jingqi, the president of the Chamber of Commerce, and Xia Canglin, the member of the Haining County Health Committee, to come to the province to petition the provincial government. According to Xia, the epidemic has been rampant for more than a month, and its scope is about dozens of miles, including Zhuqiao, Yingshumiao, Renjiacun, Shilicun, Jinshicun, Wangjiamiao, and Yuanhua, with Zhuqiao being the most prevalent. The number of deaths is about 400. Newly spread areas include Zhuqiao, Jinxianba, and Fujiaba. Other areas along the Huhang Road in Xucun, Chang'an, and Xieqiao have also been affected. The epidemic is indeed epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis. At the beginning of the disease, there is only mild headache or mild numbness in the limbs, palpitations and rapid pulse, or vomiting. Patients often do not pay attention. Severely ill people fall asleep and die within two or three hours, and some die after two or three days. The characteristics of the disease are no high fever and less opisthotonos. The pupils also do not change, and those with purplish spots on the face die at the speed of light. The bacteria seen in the examination are also larger than usual. The age of the dead is mostly from ten to thirty years old, very few are forty or fifty years old, and few are children under five years old. There are more men and fewer women. Now the Haining County Temporary Epidemic Prevention Committee has held many meetings. Two epidemic prevention stations have been set up, one in Yingshumiao and one in Zhuqiao. The isolation ward in Yingshumiao is handled by the Provincial Infectious Disease Hospital. The epidemic prevention station has organized two patrol injection teams, and burial teams, propaganda teams, and disinfection teams. More than 6,000 people have been injected with the preventive vaccine, and more than 180 people have been treated. Now that the epidemic has not subsided, I am deeply afraid that it will be even more unthinkable in the spring, so I have come to the province to petition. The secretary-general of the province, Nie, has met with them on behalf of the government. Regarding the request for relief, it will be submitted to the provincial government meeting tomorrow (20th) to discuss the solution.

Local Correspondence

Nanhui 73

A Flower Merchant's Account Leads to a Murder Case Yu Yinde from Shanghai has been selling flowers for a living. Last autumn, he collected cotton from farmers in the Shanghai area, totaling 14,000 yuan, which was all owed and not paid. Farmers repeatedly urged him to pay, so Yu avoided debts in Shanghai and dared not go home. Recently, Yu entrusted his brother Yu Jinde with 2,500 yuan to pay off the debts in order to end this matter. The content of the payments was divided into three types: 10%, 30%, and 50%. The day before yesterday, Yu Jinde invited the farmers to his home to pay off the debts and explained the reasons for the apportionment. However, the farmers felt that they were losing too much and expressed their unwillingness. Nearly a hundred people arrived at that time, and there was a lot of discussion and the order was chaotic. Yu Jinde saw that the matter was fruitless and feared that an accident would happen, so he wanted to go to the police detachment stationed there and ask them to send police to maintain order. The farmers saw that Yu was going out and feared that he would escape, so they all followed him out. When they arrived in front of the detachment, the police glanced at the large number of people and did not understand their intentions, so they fired a row of shots into the sky. However, the crowd did not retreat and fired several shots horizontally, killing a farmer named Liu Shaoqing. The crowd saw the trouble and dispersed in panic. On the one hand, they sent people to the city to file a complaint and ask for an autopsy, and asked for severe punishment for the person who caused the trouble. Yesterday, the trial officer went to the countryside for an autopsy and detained Yu Jinde, waiting for the county to try the case. The trial officer Lu ordered him to hand over his brother Yu Yinde within seven days and pay a deposit of 14,000 yuan before he could be released temporarily. However, Yu Jinde was detained pending review because he had no guarantor.

Suzhou 74

A Soil Hill Was Discovered in Jiaozhi Township Zhu Village in Jiaozhi Township, six or seven miles away from the town, suddenly had a strong wind the night before yesterday. The farmers were afraid and dared not get up. When they went out the next day, they saw a soil hill suddenly discovered in the field. It was about twenty feet in circumference and about three feet high, which was very peculiar.

The Issue of Concurrent Positions of Chamber of Commerce Committee Members The reorganization of the Suzhou General Chamber of Commerce into the Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce was held on the 15th of this month. The executive and supervisory committee members were elected, and Shi Junqing was elected as the chairman. The official establishment meeting was scheduled to be held on the 20th, but the date of establishment was postponed due to the issue of whether the newly elected committee members could concurrently hold the positions of alternate executive committee members and supervisory committee members. The Chamber of Commerce Election Law does not stipulate that it is still under study. However, the postponement date must be determined after the new chairman Shi Junqing returns to Suzhou from Beijing.

The Suzhou Area Establishes a Consolidated Tax Bureau After the elimination of the various likin cards and tax offices in Suzhou, the Finance Department sent Yi Zizhuang to Suzhou to establish a consolidated tax bureau, and found No. 1 Nanyangli as the bureau's address, and started the method immediately.

The First Day of the Trial Officer Examination The Higher Court's Trial Officer Examination was held yesterday for the first day. There were 75 candidates. The examiners were Shen Yuanhuang Bingdao, and the supervisors were Zhong Shangbin and Lai Gan. They entered the venue at 1:00 PM and left at 5:00 PM.

Wuxi 75

Telegrams Requested Interpretation of the Litigation Mediation Agency The Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce recently checked the provisions of Article 2 of the Civil Mediation Law and Article 3, Paragraph 4 of the Chamber of Commerce Law. For personnel litigation cases, the Chamber of Commerce should belong to the mediation agency for industrial and commercial operators. Yesterday, it specially telegraphed the Judicial Yuan and requested an explicit interpretation, and ordered it to be observed. It also sent telegrams to the Chambers of Commerce in Nanjing and Shanghai, and the Chambers of Commerce in the counties of Jiangsu Province, to advocate unity. The original telegram is recorded as follows: "To Wang Junjian, the President of the Nanjing Judicial Yuan, according to Article 2 of the Civil Mediation Law, personnel litigation cases and civil cases under the jurisdiction of the primary level, unless the mediation is not established by other mediation agencies, or the mediation director considers that mediation is not possible, they shall not be dismantled unless the mediation is not established by the civil mediation office. The Judiciary also stipulates in Article 6 of the matters that should be paid attention to in handling mediation that the other agencies mentioned in Article 2 of the Civil Mediation Law should be limited to those stipulated by law, such as Article 6 of the current Labor Dispute Office Law, etc. If the mediation has not been established, it should be certified by the original mediation agency, or declared by both parties, etc. Check Article 3 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, the duties of the Chamber of Commerce, Paragraph 4, matters concerning the mediation and arbitration of industry and commerce. The wording is indeed of a mediation nature. Can Article 2 of the Civil Mediation Law be applied as another mediation agency? I dare to telegraph and ask for your review, and quickly give an explicit interpretation to comply with it, so as to prevent litigation and stabilize commerce."

Meeting to Discuss the Apportionment of Silk Industry Bonds After the State Council approved the relief silk industry bonds, the amount of the bonds was changed from 10 million yuan to 7 million yuan, and recently changed to 8 million yuan. 6 million yuan will be used as a live auction to relieve silk factories, and 2 million yuan will be used to govern the root cause and run the sericulture business in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. However, for the apportionment method, each silk factory mainly apportions according to the number of cars, and a third party mainly uses exported raw silk as the standard. After the silk merchants repeatedly strived for it, they were allowed to apportion half according to the number of cars and half according to exported raw silk. Now the government has decided to start registering from the 20th of this month to the 31st of May. Fellow silk factory operators in Xidi believe that the apportionment method is still not in line with the original plan jointly decided by fellow operators in Zhejiang, Jiangsu, and Shanghai, and the third party is manipulating it. Jianglai gains and losses are of great importance. Yesterday, a special meeting was called to discuss the matter in the guild hall. More than 40 representatives from 34 factories attended. Chairman Qian Fenghao reported in detail on the progress of the case, the recent trends, and the gains and losses in the future. After discussion, everyone unanimously advocated apportioning according to the number of cars according to the original plan, and asked the representatives to Shanghai this time to strive for it with all their strength. If necessary, all factories in Wuxi will go to Shanghai to petition, in order to achieve the goal of truly relieving silk factories and the majority of workers.

Changzhou 76

Middle School Students Strike in Wujin County. More than three months have passed since Zhuang Chen was appointed as the principal of the Wujin County Junior Middle School. According to news today (the 19th), all students of the school went on strike last Friday due to issues such as the refund of leftover meal fees and the answers to physics questions. On Saturday, the first and second-year students also unanimously went on strike, causing the unrest to escalate. Principal Zhuang Chen reported the situation to the Education Bureau on the 18th, requesting instructions on how to proceed.

Cargo Ship Robbed Near the City. A cargo ship from Jiangbei was moored along the Nanhe River outside the West Gate of Wuyi. The shipowner, Tang Lishu, had collected money the day before in preparation for traveling elsewhere. Unexpectedly, at around 4 a.m. on the 18th, four armed bandits suddenly appeared, robbing all the cargo, more than 160 yuan in foreign currency, and clothing, before fleeing.

Zhenjiang 77

Change of Head of the Bank of Communications. Zhu Baoheng, the head of the Zhenjiang Bank of Communications, has resigned. The vacancy has been filled by Yan Dunxian, who was specially invited by the head office to take over.

Continued Interrogation in the Flower Girl Poisoning Case. In the case of the prostitute Hua Xiren (also known as Lu Fengzhen) committing suicide by poisoning, Li Changyi and Li Houpei, who had close ties with Hua, were detained by the Fifth Precinct, and the court was notified to send a prosecutor. Together with forensic officials, they went to Shengshou Temple for an examination. Lu Xuemei (Hua's uncle), a relative, rushed to request exemption from the examination. Li and others confessed to the Fifth Precinct that Hua committed suicide due to heartbreak. However, in her suicide note, Hua stated that she went to Li Changyi's place to withdraw 1,600 yuan in savings, but he refused to pay. In addition, her lover went elsewhere, leading her to take her own life. Li and others have now been transferred by the Fifth Precinct to the court for interrogation. Lu Xuemei will also be prosecuted.

Nantong 78

Investigation Confirms Misconduct of the Director of the Construction Bureau. The Construction Department has repeatedly received accusations from local people against Yao Pengnian, the director of the Construction Bureau, for various acts of embezzlement and misconduct. Yu Dingming was appointed to conduct a thorough investigation in Tongzhou. When Yu requested to review the account books from Yao, Yao refused to hand them over. Yu telegraphed the department for instructions. On the 17th, a telegram was received in reply, ordering Yao to hand over the books immediately and warning that severe penalties would be imposed if he dared to conceal or delay. After Yao handed over the accounts, Yu discovered that he had embezzled public funds, including 1,673 yuan from the ordinary automobile donation and 200 yuan from the Dasheng Yarn Factory's subsidy for Yuejiang Road. Yao, realizing that his misdeeds had been exposed, left Tongzhou that night.

Escape from the Kidnapping Case at Luhong Lock. A kidnapping case occurred at Luhong Lock in the south of the city. The six male and female hostages have been missing for two months. Recently, Lu Hongquan, the bookkeeper of the pig trade, and his wife, Wu Huangshi, escaped from a pirate ship in Lvsi and returned to the city. It is said that they were redeemed for 4,500 yuan. Another victim, a Mr. Yin, the owner of a timber business, is being held for a ransom of 10,000 yuan, and negotiations are underway.

Hangzhou 79

Mortgaging Foil Business Tax for Loans. The Zhejiang Finance Department convened a discussion meeting yesterday to continue negotiating loans. As a result, all old debts owed to the province and their collaterals will continue to be maintained according to the previous contracts. For the new loan, it was originally proposed to mortgage 2.3 million in three types of debt tax coupons to borrow 2 million in cash. However, with the implementation of the abolition of likin, it is difficult to establish this. After repeated consultations, it was changed to mortgage 2.2 million in foil business tax from the entire province for the new debt. Banking circles have expressed their agreement, so the loan is expected to be established within days.

High Court Pardons Political Prisoners. The Zhejiang High Court was ordered to handle matters related to the general amnesty. After reviewing the political prisoners detained in the court, it was approved by the central government for pardon and they have all been released. The names of the sixteen released political prisoners are listed below: Zeng Zuxi, Zeng Zuheng, Cao Peng, Sun Youfu, Wang Baoan, Chen Xingsun, Wu Jinbing, Kong Xiangshui, Chen Zhen, Zhang Yuntao, Zhou Zhengwen, Zhao Shouwan, Zhang Yaoying, Zhang Mosen, Zhou Guoling, Lu Jiamu.

Fengxian 80

Proposal to Merge Taiping Township. The proposal to merge Taiping Township in Nanhui has been discussed repeatedly without a result. Now, local gentry Jiang Jie and others have reiterated the previous proposal at this county administrative meeting. The reasons are roughly as follows: the area of the township extends from Zhangang in the east to Qianbu Jing in the west, a total of more than twenty li in length from east to west, and about three li from north to south. It is an important channel for the seven vertical trunk rivers of our Fengxian to flow into the sea, and also the throat of the entire county. However, due to this relationship, obstacles arise in administration. For example, in terms of arrests, the bandits who burned and looted Zhuangxing the year before all hid in the township. In the kidnapping and robbery cases in the past few months, the township has also been a den for hiding. The southern bandits are unable to fully govern due to their limited resources, while our county is limited by the county boundary and cannot search and suppress them, resulting in it gradually becoming a hotbed of all evils. Therefore, merging it into Fengxian is a matter of urgent importance and will achieve the effect of limbs and arms coordinating. It is understood that after the case was passed by the general meeting, County Magistrate Shen Qingchen added a letter of explanation yesterday, along with boundary maps, and submitted it to the provincial civil construction departments for instructions.

Pensions for Descendants of Original Donors to Charities. Dong Zhiliang, a descendant of the original donors to the Qingcun Port Infant Asylum, recently intended to recover the fields donated to the asylum by his ancestors to manage them himself to supplement his studies and meals due to his family's financial difficulties. The asylum considered the matter to be unprecedented, so it requested the county for approval the day before. It is now understood that the county has approved the case, stating that the fields have long been donated for the purpose of feeding the poor, so the right to manage them should belong to the relief organization. The request for personal management cannot be approved. However, considering the relationship as descendants of the original donors and the fact that the family is indeed poor, appropriate subsidies should be given to show compassion. At the same time, it was decided at the county political meeting that in addition to the annual allocation of 100 yuan for pensions from the field rents, each of his three children will receive an additional 50 yuan per year for tuition fees to promote their education.

Letter from Lin & Co., No. 39 Sichuan Road, This City 81

Dear Sirs,

In the Wuxi correspondence column of your newspaper on the 16th of this month, it was stated that the seven silk factories in Wuxi, including Shengyu, Wansheng No. 1 and No. 2 factories (mistakenly written as Yisheng), Jintai, Ruifu, and Taifu, all contracted with Lin & Co. in Shanghai to supply coal for their use. However, recently, the company has failed to deliver the coal, causing the seven silk factories to have no coal to burn and unable to operate, resulting in the unemployment of tens of thousands of workers. This is inconsistent with the facts. It is hereby clarified that our company signed coal supply contracts with silk factories such as Shengyu, stipulating the pricing standards and payment dates. If the silk factories fail to pay according to the contract, our company is entitled to suspend coal delivery and demand compensation for losses. After the contracts were established, our company supplied coal according to the contracts and never caused any coal shortages for the silk factories. However, the silk factories have been inexplicably underpaying or delaying payments without reason, failing to pay despite repeated reminders and ignoring mediation efforts. Our company needs funds to purchase coal, and our capital is at stake. We cannot afford to compensate for losses, so we had no choice but to declare the termination of the contracts in accordance with the contract terms. The factories have instead claimed that our company breached the contract by failing to supply coal, causing the silk factories to be unable to operate and resulting in the unemployment of tens of thousands of workers, spreading this message everywhere. It is not known that some of these factories only operate for ten to twenty days a month, while others have already ceased operations due to the decline in silk prices and their own failure. How is this related to our company? Moreover, there are many coal companies. If the factories have money, they can purchase coal from other companies for burning. There is no reason for labor disputes to arise simply because the contracts with our company have been terminated. The correspondence in your newspaper is contrary to the facts and affects our company's reputation. We hereby send this letter to clarify the facts and request a fair correction.

Sincerely,

Lin & Co., Shanghai

Local News

American Chamber of Commerce Opposes Silver Loan to China 82

Already Telegraphed to the U.S. Department of Commerce

According to the Da Mei Evening News, the American Chamber of Commerce in this city has telegraphed the U.S. Department of Commerce in Washington, stating that providing a silver loan to China at this time would be harmful and unhelpful to the Chinese market and trade with China and foreign countries. This telegram is in response to the proposal by Senator Pittman and the International Silver Committee to lend 20 million taels of silver to China to promote trade with China and foreign countries. The American Chamber of Commerce believes that China still needs to pay in gold for purchasing goods from abroad, and this type of loan is of no benefit to trade with China and foreign countries. After a thorough discussion among the leaders of the American Chamber of Commerce in this city, this telegram was sent to oppose the silver loan.

Location of County Seat Confirmed 83

Resolution of the Shanghai County Relocation Promotion Meeting

The Shanghai County Relocation Promotion Meeting held a joint meeting of standing committee members and design committee members at the Beiqiao Third District Office on the 18th. The attending committee members included Wang Chengyao, Niu Changyao, Peng Zhaotang, Peng Liren, Ge Xiusheng, Sun Shiben, Yang Fulin, Ni Binzhi, and others, totaling eight people. First, the chairman reported, and Committee Member Niu Yongjian reported on the situation of contacting the provincial and municipal governments and his opinions on the design of the new county seat. Then, discussions began and the following important cases were resolved: (1) Regarding the area of the new county seat base, it was resolved to provisionally set it at 200 mu, with 50 mu purchased first in the central area. (2) Regarding the confirmation of the county seat base, it was resolved to designate approximately 50 mu to the east of Hu-Min Road, west of Hengjing, and north of Beitang Road as the county seat center, and approximately 150 mu of fields in the two districts west of Hu-Min Road and east of Hengjing as the county seat base. It is also heard that the land price for the county seat has also been determined.

Inauguration of the Shanghai County Relocation Design Committee

Minutes of the First Meeting

The issue of relocating the Shanghai County seat has been addressed by the establishment of a Design Committee comprised of fifteen committee members, tasked with deliberating and advancing the project. Yesterday morning at ten o'clock, the committee members convened at the County Government auditorium for their inauguration ceremony. Attendees included committee members Shi She, Wang Li, Peng Zhaotang, Peng Liren, Wu Wenhua, Ye Dezhen, Lu Zhe, Niu Changyao, Ge Xiusheng, Shen Zhou, Yang Fulin, Wang Chengyao, and Bi Huan, totaling thirteen individuals. Absent were Qin Xitian and Wu Jingqing. Following the inauguration ceremony, the committee members initiated their inaugural meeting, chaired by Wu Wenhua with Li Tongrui serving as the recording secretary. After customary formalities, Chairman Wu Wenhua delivered an introductory address, highlighting that since the division of Shanghai into county and municipality, the original county seat, situated within the municipal area, had posed considerable challenges to administrative operations. Therefore, for the sake of operational efficiency, the relocation of the Shanghai County seat had become a consensus demand between the government and the populace. Former County Magistrate Lu had previously outlined plans, but due to various unresolved issues, the project had been suspended. Since taking office, County Magistrate Yan had given significant attention to this matter, resulting in a resolution by the fifty-fourth County Council meeting to establish a Design Committee to oversee the project. With this inaugural meeting, it was hoped that all members would contribute their opinions and engage in collaborative discussions to ensure the swift realization of this relocation plan, as deeply desired. Subsequently, the committee deliberated and resolved various matters: (1) Approval of the Detailed Rules for the Committee's Operations, passed with revisions. Cases two and three are omitted. (4) Regarding the date for on-site surveys of the County Seat location, it was resolved to schedule it for ten o'clock in the morning on the 31st of this month. The meeting adjourned at nearly twelve o'clock.

Appendix: Detailed Rules for the Design Committee's Operations. (Article 1) These Detailed Rules are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 12 of the Committee's Constitution. (Article 2) The Chairman, in addition to presiding over meetings, shall oversee all internal affairs of the Committee. (Article 3) The Director of General Affairs shall consult with the Chairman to handle the internal affairs of the Committee. (Article 4) In the event of the Chairman's absence due to unforeseen circumstances, an interim chairperson may be elected from among the committee members present. (Article 5) The Chairman shall assign the duties of full-time Committee staff. (Article 6) Committee members shall, in principle, attend meetings daily. (Article 7) The meeting time shall be announced in advance by the Chairman. (Article 8) Before the meeting, the recording staff shall prepare the agenda and compile and distribute draft resolutions to all Committee members. (Article 9) Committee members submitting proposals requiring written explanation should submit them to the Chairman before the meeting. (Article 10) When necessary, consultants may be notified to attend discussions, but they shall have no voting rights. (Article 11) Any matters not fully covered by these Detailed Rules shall be resolved by the Committee through discussion and amendment. (Article 12) These Detailed Rules shall be implemented upon passage by the Committee.

The Third and Fourth Meetings of the Two-Railways Business Conference Were Held Yesterday 84

Eighty-Eight Proposals from Various Groups Were Resolved

Zheng Baozhao Reported on the Income and Expenditure of the Two Railways

The Closing Ceremony Will Be Held This Afternoon to Issue a Declaration

The Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Two-Railways Business Conference held its third meeting at 9:30 a.m. yesterday, discussing the first review report without resolving all the cases. The fourth meeting continued from 2:00 p.m. to discuss the second review report on transportation, station affairs, and freight. 124 representatives and experts from various regions attended, with Liu Chengchang as the chairman and Cai Qianjun as the recorder. The situation yesterday is recorded below:

The Morning General Meeting 85

Discussion Situation: After the meeting opened yesterday morning, the secretariat first reported on the resolutions of the second general meeting. Then, based on the review report, the station affairs group was discussed, starting from case 182, and the second review report ended at case 25. The road bureau made reports or explanations on various cases. The details are as follows: (1) Case 61: Representative Zheng Baozhao from the road bureau reported that the monthly expenditure of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway is 400,000 (including road maintenance costs). The principal of the loan to the Sino-British Company is 75,000 pounds, and the interest payment is 30,000 pounds and some change. The daily income of the road bureau is only over 10,000. The freight cost is 1.1%, and the passenger cost is 0.95%, which may increase to 1.2% from the 20th. Reducing freight rates is impossible. Case 65: The road bureau reported that the current transportation price of silk is 0.6% per ton per kilometer, which has now increased to 0.8%. The Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway charges 50% of the freight rate, and the Beijing-Shanghai Railway charges 2.25 yuan for items within 60 kilograms. Case 23: The road bureau reported that the baggage package rate is 6.25 jiao per 50 kilograms, which is doubled instead of increasing by half. The actual calculation is only 0.168. Extension of the Meeting Period: At the morning general meeting yesterday, it was proposed to extend the meeting period, which was approved by the public decision. The fourth general meeting will continue to be held from 3:00 p.m. today (the 19th) to continue discussing the review report. Review meetings of various groups will be held that evening to review all cases that have not been submitted to the general meeting for resolution in the agenda for the 19th.

Resolutions of Various Cases: First Review Report (Station Affairs Group) Case 183: Amended and passed according to the review opinions. The case is reserved and the road bureau is requested to contact the various transfer companies to handle it. Case 84 passed. (Freight Group) Case 48: Amended and passed according to the review opinions. (1) Regarding the reduction of the grade of miscellaneous goods and piece goods, it seems that there is a reason why it cannot be reduced further. (A) The current freight rate for domestically produced piece goods transported from Shanghai South Station to Hangzhou is 3.734 yuan per ton. For imported piece goods, the freight rate is 6.506 yuan per ton, which is 2.77 yuan more expensive. The road bureau has specially reduced the freight rate for domestically produced piece goods. (B) There are many types of miscellaneous goods, and they can be shipped separately, charging fees according to the freight rates of each grade. Merchants should not suffer losses. (2) Regarding the addition of special trains during the tea cocoon transportation period, if there are sufficient locomotives, the road bureau may be requested to consider adding special trains. Cases 49 to 61 were all passed according to the original text of the review report. Case 62 was amended and passed. The reason why it cannot be reduced further is that the new chapter price has already been reduced. The transportation costs of the two railways are different, and it is difficult to equalize the freight rates. Cases 63 to 66, and 65 were passed in their original text. Cases 67 and 51 were amended and passed according to the review opinions. The transportation cost of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway is very high, and no profit can be obtained below the fourth-class price, and paper goods are mostly within the fourth and fifth-class prices. It does not seem appropriate to reduce the freight rates, but regarding the statement in the original proposal that most of the paper goods are transported by water, it is proposed that the road bureau send personnel to investigate the actual situation and formulate appropriate measures to attract more customers. Case 68 was passed in its original text. Second Review Report (Transportation Group) Case 19: Passed according to the review results in its original text. The congestion of passengers in the Xichang section is a fact, but according to the report of the road bureau, it is due to the reduction in the traction of the locomotive, and the vehicles towed by each train have reached the maximum limit, so passenger cars cannot be added. However, to avoid congestion, the road bureau should try its best to find a solution within a possible range. Regarding the hygiene on the train, the road bureau reported that hygiene inspectors have been dispatched to check at any time, and attendants are on the train to provide services. The road bureau should strictly order these personnel to seriously handle the hygiene on the train. Case 20 is the same as case 19. Case 21 was passed after review. According to the report of the road bureau, the addition of freight cars is difficult due to the limited traction of the locomotive. However, the time for fresh goods is important, and the road bureau should try to arrange transportation as soon as possible. Case 22 was passed after review. The direct passenger train to Beijing and Shanghai has as many as 19 passenger cars. If freight cars are added, it is also limited by the locomotive power and it is difficult to handle. However, regional trains can be added, and the road bureau should do so. As for the improvement of vehicles for loading fresh goods, there is a solution in case 7. Case 23 was passed after review. This case requested the slow train to tow chestnuts, dates, and Gorgon fruit. The review method is the same as the first section of case 22. As for the request to waive the half-price freight rate, it has been transferred to the Freight Group Review Committee for review. Case 24 was passed after review. The road bureau should earnestly handle the prompt allocation of vehicles. As for the responsibility for freight transportation, it should be incorporated into the review of cases 97, 98, 99, and 100. Case 25 was passed after review. According to the report of the road bureau, although there was a lack of vehicles during the military period, the road has made great efforts to maintain commercial transportation. Now that the military situation has ended, and the road has decided to add 200 freight cars, measures should be taken to adjust the vehicles for commercial transportation in the future, so that transportation can be smooth. The committee believes that this method of the road bureau is complete and should be earnestly handled by the road bureau.

Afternoon Fourth Session 86

Discussion Circumstances: The fourth session of the conference continued from 2 PM, starting with the discussion of the 26 proposals from the Transportation Group. All review reports from the three groups were approved unanimously, with no disputes among the representatives. Progress was smooth. It was decided that after the adjournment, the Review Committee and the Declaration Drafting Committee would continue their work. The designated review committee members included Mr. Zheng Baozhao, the representative from the Railway Bureau. He reported during the meeting that the monthly expenditure of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway (including road maintenance costs) was 720,000 yuan, with an annual repayment of £116,000 and interest of £69,600. Daily revenue was over 30,000 yuan. The freight charge per kilometer per ton was 6.06 cents, and passenger transport was 6.6 cents, which will increase to 8 cents to 1 cent in twenty years. Comparing freight rates for 312 kilometers between Shanghai and Nanjing, the fare was 1 yuan, 5 jiao, 4 fen, 3 li, 2 hao; Tianjin-Pukou was 3 yuan, 0 fen, 6 li, 2 hao; Beijing-Liaoning was 3 yuan, 1 jiao, 7 fen; Longhai was 3 yuan, 5 jiao, 0 fen, 8 li; and Beijing-Hankou was 9 yuan, 1 jiao, 6 fen, all showing increases.

Resolutions on Various Proposals: Proposal No. 26 from the "Transportation Group" was approved after review. (1) Regarding the allocation of five carriages daily, it was noted that empty carriages at Wusong Station were allocated from Ma Station, and the number of loaded carriages arriving at Ma Station daily varied. It was difficult to specify a fixed number. However, given the importance of coal transportation for various factories, the Railway Bureau should try its best to facilitate this within its capabilities. However, to facilitate commerce, the Railway Bureau should consider appropriate measures. Proposal No. 28 was approved after review, requesting the Railway Bureau to allocate as many carriages as possible. Proposal No. 29 was approved after review, noting that it was difficult to specify the number of carriages to be allocated daily, but requesting the Railway Bureau to allocate as many as possible. Proposal No. 30 was the same as Proposal No. 28. Proposal No. 31 was the same as Proposal No. 3. Proposal No. 32 was approved after review. The number of freight cars on both railways was explained in the overview of the scheduling of passenger and freight cars on both lines. There was no detention of vehicles during the period of military pacification. Proposal No. 33 was approved after review. The railway has now decided to lease 100 freight cars, and should allocate sufficient cars in the future to avoid delays. Proposal No. 123 was approved after review, requesting the Railway Bureau to find ways to expand it. Regarding the issue of adding tarpaulins, the Railway Bureau should consider adding some to meet urgent needs. (2) The station lights are already being installed by the Railway Bureau. (3) Covering the overpass seems necessary, and the Railway Bureau should consider it. Proposal No. 141 was approved after review, noting that the land east of Songjiang Station belongs to the Railway Bureau and is not a branch road. The committee is not in a position to discuss whether the coal layer should be removed. Proposal No. 142 was approved after review, requesting the Railway Bureau to consider extending it. Proposal No. 143 was approved after review, requesting the Railway Bureau to first consider extending the awning at the station name. As for the awning on the opposite platform, it must wait until the Railway Bureau is financially sound before further consideration. Proposal No. 144 was approved after review, requesting the Railway Bureau to plan the expansion of fire-fighting equipment on the entire line to prevent accidents. Proposal No. 161 was approved after review, noting that the location for cargo delivery must be based on the customer's wishes, and the Railway Bureau should not interfere. Therefore, if the customer needs to change the unloading location, please contact the Railway Bureau directly. Further discussion is needed. Proposal No. 164 was approved after review, finding that the station where goods are loaded and unloaded is determined by the customer, and the Railway Bureau cannot restrict it. This case cannot be established. Proposal No. 174 was approved after review: A. The land at Ma Station has always been swept and cleaned by the cargo owners themselves. The remaining land has been contracted to Yu Yongtai, and the revenue is collected by the Railway Bureau's accounting department, not divided between superiors and subordinates. B. A cement wall has already been built on the north side of the station, and building it on the south side would be too expensive and difficult. The Railway should issue a notice to the railway police to strictly prevent and prohibit unauthorized personnel from entering. C. Numbering barges falls within the scope of municipal administration, and the Railway Bureau is unable to handle this matter. This item is not suitable for discussion. Proposal No. 69 from the "Freight Rate Group" was approved after review, noting that Chinese and foreign goods have different grades, and the grade of domestic goods is already lower. Proposal No. 70 was approved after review, noting that the freight rate for native cloth is already low, reduced by half compared to before, and does not need to be reduced further. Proposal No. 71 was approved after review, noting that this matter concerns all railways in the country. The original proposer should prepare a detailed list of raw materials and submit it to the Ministry of Industry, which will forward it to the Ministry of Railways for review. Proposal No. 72 was approved after review, noting that the current 50-kilogram freight rate is already half lower than before, and cannot be reduced further. Proposal No. 73 was approved after review, finding that large quantities of rice, wheat, and flour are transported from Wuhu to Shanghai by ice transport. To recover this loss, the Railway Bureau is requested to consider reducing the freight rate for these goods. Proposal No. 74 was approved after review, finding that the freight rate for soybean oil from Changzhou to Ningbo under the old regulations was 1 yuan, 3 jiao, 5 fen per ton, plus 10% making it 1 yuan, 4 jiao, 8 fen, 5 hao. The new regulations are 1 yuan, 5 jiao, 1 fen, 7 hao, a difference of 2 fen, and there is no need for further reduction. Proposal No. 75 was approved after review, merging this case with Case No. 72. Proposal No. 76 was approved after review, noting that the new regulations for less-than-carload freight rates are already low and do not need to be revised. Proposal No. 77 was approved after review, finding that the Railway Bureau's current freight rates are already 3% lower than before and do not need to be reduced further. Proposal No. 78 was approved after review, noting that the Railway Bureau is currently purchasing more locomotives and there will be no problems in the future. The current freight rate for fourth-class goods is already lower than cost and cannot be reduced further. Proposal No. 79 was approved after review, merging this case with Case No. 75. Proposal No. 80 was approved after review, finding that the Railway Bureau's prices have been revised and implemented since January of this year and are already lower than before and cannot be reduced further. Proposal No. 81 was approved after review, finding that most of the freight from Songjiang is less-than-carload, which is already low. As for the cost of collecting and delivering goods, it has always been handled by the customers themselves, and the customers should directly consult with the contractor at that station to negotiate a reduction. Proposal No. 82 was approved after review, merging this case with Case No. 73. Proposal No. 83 was approved after review, noting that the new price is reduced by half compared to the old price, so it cannot be reduced further. Proposal No. 84 was approved after review, noting that there are special prices for shipping cotton yarn. Please ask the Railway Bureau to consider it after the period expires. It was also found that the Railway Bureau's labor fees for loading and unloading have slightly increased to maintain the workers' livelihood due to the rising cost of living in various places. Proposal No. 85 was approved after review, finding that the third-class passenger fare from Suzhou to Shanghai is 9 jiao per person, which is 1 fen per kilometer. This amount is only enough to cover the cost of railway transportation, so it cannot be reduced further. Proposal No. 86 was approved after review, proposing that the Railway Bureau transport oilcloth, canvas, and empty bags used for packaging silk back to the starting station free of charge. Proposal No. 87 was approved after review, merging this case with Case No. 86. According to the original proposal, all have already been reported on the 17th, and are slightly omitted due to space constraints.)

Silk and Satin Industry Requests Light or Exempt Taxes 88

Trade Association Cables for Vigorous Advocacy

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Representatives Go to Beijing to Request Exemption

Municipal Silk and Satin Industry: The Municipal Silk and Satin Industry Trade Association, due to the implementation of the abolition of likin, will implement a business tax to compensate for provincial revenue. At this critical time for the silk and satin industry, the government is requested to provide relief and reduce the suffering of silk merchants. A telegram was sent to the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Business Tax Discussion Committee, requesting them to preside over the matter, and a letter was sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Hangzhou Silk Industry Trade Association, requesting them to jointly advocate for this. The text reads: (Titles Omitted) Likin is a detrimental policy that has plagued merchants for a long time. Recently, our government has issued a clear order to abolish it, and the national industry and commerce sectors all believe that they have been freed from shackles and are rejoicing in unison. However, after the abolition of likin, a business tax must be implemented to compensate for revenue. According to reports, the tax rate for silk fabrics in the business regulations of your province is 30 per mille of the business turnover. Moreover, the Executive Yuan recently issued a general order stipulating that the outline of the business tax should not exceed 20 per mille at most. Comparing the two, they are already different. It is speculated that the intention is to regard silk fabrics as luxury goods, and therefore impose a tax exceeding the normal limit. All of our silk merchants are shocked. We believe that clothing and housing are the primary needs of human life. For clothing, cloth and silk are complementary. Exquisite clothing cannot consist entirely of cloth and exclude silk. Our country's silk cloth is like foreign woolen fabrics. Since other countries do not consider woolen fabrics as luxury goods, our country's silk fabrics should naturally be considered daily necessities and should not be listed as luxuries, first point. China is founded on agriculture, and sericulture is the primary agricultural product. Jiangsu and Zhejiang have always been known as prosperous regions because they produce excellent silk. Countless farmers, workers, and merchants in Jiangsu and Zhejiang rely on this for their livelihood. However, since silk from Japan and Vietnam is encroaching upon Chinese silk, our country's silk export proportion has been declining daily. The Chinese people are also increasingly fascinated by Europeanization, regarding imported silk and woolen fabrics as the supreme treasures, while turning Chinese silk into worn-out shoes. As a result, the silk industry has lost its original exit externally and is being overshadowed by imports internally, leading to a decline to a low point and near death. The Chinese people are running around calling for help, seeking to rescue it. If we were to regard it as a luxury and impose heavy taxes on it, it would only hasten its demise. This is the second point that silk fabrics should not be listed as luxuries. The silk industry has suffered from labor disputes, foreign aggression, likin exploitation, and transportation obstacles. For the sake of promoting sales, we sell at parity prices and dare not seek profit. For every 1,000 yuan of goods, excluding the cost of capital, the net profit is less than 3%. Heavy tax burdens are far beyond our ability to bear. Furthermore, the government's abolition of likin was originally intended to rescue industry and the people's livelihood. If we regard it as a luxury, it would not only contradict the original intention of abolishing likin but would also mean escaping from shackles only to be placed in a yoke. The closing of silk factories is bound to follow one after another, and the consequences are unimaginable. This is the third point that silk fabrics should not be listed as luxuries. At this critical time for the silk industry, silk merchants are looking forward to the government's tax exemption relief. Even if it is to compensate for the provincial treasury and implement a business tax, it should be reduced as much as possible to alleviate the people's suffering. We request that domestic silk be regarded as domestic woolen fabrics, and the business tax be set at 2 per mille. Then, silk merchants can fulfill their duty to contribute, and the government will not be accused of increasing the burden. Regarding all the reasons why silk fabrics should not be listed as luxuries and should be given special tax relief, we jointly cable our request to your office, asking you to sympathize with the difficulties of the merchants and grant relief to maintain the silk merchants and benefit the people's livelihood. We are deeply grateful. The Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Trade Association respectfully kowtows.

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry: The Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Weaving Joint Association, regarding the issue of changing the tax on domestic silk to a special consumption tax, specifically convened representatives of silk industry groups from both provinces yesterday to hold a plenary session of representatives at the association. Wang Jiean was elected as chairman, and rituals were performed accordingly. The chairman announced the purpose of the meeting and described the various difficulties of the national silk industry, facing internal and external pressures and nearing death. Now that the national government is determined to abolish likin and cultivate the people's livelihood, our silk industry should seize the opportunity to discuss and resolve the painful and recuperating measures, and submit them to the national government for adoption and implementation to rescue the industry. Subsequently, Cheng Ganqing, Wang Xingyi, Wu Xingcha, Tao Shunan, and others successively expressed their opinions, and all agreed that each group should designate representatives to form a petition delegation to go to Beijing to visit the national government departments, requesting consideration for the silk industry's imminent crisis, and temporarily granting a three-year exemption from silk tax. This was unanimously approved by the entire body, and Wang Jiean was elected as the chief representative of the petition. The Wuxian Yarn and Silk Industry Association nominated Cheng Ganqing, Shi Jianqing, and Chen Guiting; the Suzhou Iron Machine Silk Weaving Association nominated Liu Fuqing and Lu Jigao; the Waiyang Silk Shop Association nominated Zhou Lianbo; the Shanghai Electric Machine Silk Weaving Association nominated Shen Tianxin and Gao Shiheng; and the Shengjing Silk Industry Office nominated Wu Xingcha and Yang Junnan. The respective representatives have already embarked on their journey to Beijing to petition for tax exemption.

New Ningxing Stranded 89

Water at Taishi Reef Only Ten Feet

Waking Lion Tugboat Rescues New Ningxing

He Chengjun and Xia Douyin Delayed

He Chengjun, Chairman of Hubei Province, and Xia Douyin, Commander of the Wuhan Garrison, were going to Beijing to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to discuss the suppression of bandits. They were traveling on the Sansui New Ningxing steamer eastward when the ship ran aground in the Anhui Province section of the Yangtze River, causing a delay for He and Xia. The report of this matter is as follows:

New Ningxing Stranded: The Sansui Company's Yangtze River steamer New Ningxing was returning to Shanghai from Wuhan, carrying a large amount of cargo. The water level in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River was low. When the ship reached Anqing, the river water was eleven feet deep. Upon reaching Taishi Reef near Anqing, the water was only ten feet deep. The ship, with too much draft, ran aground and was unable to move.

He and Xia Delayed: He Xuezhu, Chairman of Hubei Province, and Xia Douyin, Commander of the Wuhan Garrison, were summoned to Beijing by Chairman Chiang to discuss the suppression of bandits. They boarded the New Ningxing eastward. When the ship ran aground, He and Xia were extremely anxious, fearing that they would be delayed in their official duties. They ordered the shipowner to send a telegram to Shanghai and Hankou for help. After the shipowner sent a second telegram for assistance, the Hongli was sent to tug the ship.

Sansui Sends Tugboats: Upon receiving the report, the Sansui Shanghai office urgently telegraphed all ships in transit to go to the rescue. At that time, the upper Yangtze River steamer Hongli was first alerted and rushed from Datong to Taishi Reef to tug the ship. After three or four hours, the New Ningxing was deeply mired in the mud and was difficult to pull out. While there was no solution, the Dexing, which had launched in Hankou, received this news and immediately rushed to the scene of the accident. The Dexing tried its best to tow the New Ningxing, but it had already been stranded for a day and a half. However, the river water was too shallow and the ship was too heavily laden, so countless attempts to tow it were still ineffective. The shipowner then consulted with He Chengjun and Xia Douyin, fearing that the New Ningxing could not be freed in time and would delay official business, and requested that the two officials transfer to the Dexing to go to Beijing first. At that time, a sampan was lowered, carrying He and Xia to the Dexing. It was estimated that they would arrive in the capital last night, but they had already been delayed by two days en route.

Waking Lion Successfully Rescues the Ship: After the Dexing left, the company's Waking Lion was sent empty to Taishi Reef for towing. By the morning of yesterday, the river water had risen greatly. The Waking Lion used a lasso to pull the New Ningxing with force, finally freeing it. It is not yet known whether the bottom of the ship was damaged. It will be necessary to wait until the ship returns to Shanghai tomorrow and unloads its cargo before inspecting the bottom of the ship.

Zhao Tiehan Cables Request to Severely Punish the Culprits in the Zhao Case 90

Request to Handle the Case Like the Chen Case

Zhao Tiehan's telegram to the Central Government reads: To the National Government of Nanjing, Central Party Headquarters, Executive Yuan, and Commander-in-Chief Chiang, Upon reading the news that the murderers of my late brother Zhao Tieqiao, the former special commissioner of the National Government for reorganizing the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, including Xia Shaoen, have been transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for trial as instructed by the Executive Yuan. However, upon investigation, the court's procedures are numerous and prone to delays, which may make it difficult to uncover the truth and lead to a miscarriage of justice. When can the truth be revealed? My late brother Tieqiao followed the Premier for over twenty years, running around for the revolution, experiencing many hardships. He served the government, took over the management of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, eliminated long-standing malpractices, spared no effort, recovered aviation rights, was not afraid of violence, insisted on integrity, and did not accept money, sacrificing himself to repay the Party and the country. During the campaign to suppress Li and Bai, he worked hard on military transport and made minor contributions. Previously, he was assassinated and died in his post. We should request the government to recall his previous services and handle the case of the assassination of the late martyr Chen Yingshi, submitting the murderers Xia Shaoen and others to a special court or to the military court of the headquarters of the army, navy, and air force, to investigate the instigators and publicly pronounce the punishment. This would not only clear the name of the deceased but also ensure the protection of all officials who work hard for the government and are happy to serve. Respectfully, Zhao Tiehan kowtows. Seal.

Dispute over the Commercial Press 91

The Social Bureau's Mediation of the Internal Organization of the Commercial Press: Divided into four parts: General Affairs Department, Distribution Office, Translation and Compilation Office, and Printing Office. General Manager Wang Yunwu, in order to reorganize internally, stipulated: (1) "Trial Regulations for Work Remuneration Standards" for the Translation and Compilation Office, meaning that translators and compilers, who were previously paid monthly salaries, would now be paid according to the amount of work they completed. The translation and compilation work was divided into eight grades, with the lowest paid 2 yuan per thousand characters and the highest paid 6 yuan per thousand characters. (2) At the Printing Office, after the workers started work at 8:10 am, the gate would be closed, prohibiting workers from freely entering and exiting, except in the following necessary circumstances: (A) Personal illness, (B) Negligence by neighbors, (C) Serious illness of parents or spouse. (3) The attendance sheet for the letterpress printing department was revised, and a survey form was added to be compared with the attendance sheet. The employees were dissatisfied with all of the above points, and the atmosphere became increasingly tense. Subsequently, the Social Bureau summoned employee representatives for questioning last Thursday and implemented mediation the day before yesterday (the 17th). The employee union side sent eight representatives in total, including Chen Yuesheng and Wan Pusheng from the General Affairs Department, Zhu Gongchui and Feng Yixian from the Translation and Compilation Office, Wang Yongliang and Shen Shifang from the Distribution Office, and Yang Youren and Wang Changyuan from the Printing Office. Among the eight representatives, Wang Changyuan and Chen Yuesheng were appointed as the chief representatives. Xu Zhi, a staff member of the Third Section of the Social Bureau, mediated the dispute. The results were: (1) The Printing Office's practice of closing the factory gate on time to prevent theft was deemed legitimate. However, the employees could propose reasonable conditions to alleviate the difficulties. The representatives then proposed five conditions: (A) Employees requesting leave to leave the factory during work hours would not be limited to the existing conditions (i.e., the original three conditions). (B) A reception room would be set up for relatives and friends to visit, and the inspector would notify them for a meeting. (C) The armed police at the factory gate should not interfere with the employees; if intervention is necessary, it should be handled by the inspector. (D) Employees who come to the factory for medical treatment should be allowed to enter and not be hindered. (E) There would be no time limit for employees to request leave. The company agreed to accept the above five conditions. (2) The two sides held opposing views on the trial implementation of the new work remuneration standard for the Translation and Compilation Office, and mediation was unsuccessful. It was decided that mediation would be conducted again today (the 20th). If mediation fails today, the matter will be submitted to arbitration. (3) The attendance sheet for the letterpress printing department was revised, and a survey form was added, but the old regulations will be temporarily followed. The General Affairs, Translation and Compilation, Distribution, and Printing Offices held an emergency joint meeting of representatives from 2:00 pm to 4:30 pm yesterday afternoon, deciding to send four representatives to attend the Social Bureau's mediation today, and to issue a declaration in the Translation and Compilation Office, with the other three offices issuing declarations of support simultaneously, and then the four offices issuing a joint declaration.

The Employee Union's Reception: The employee union of the Translation and Compilation Office of the Commercial Press hosted guests from all walks of life at Yizhixiang Restaurant last night at 7:00 pm. Chairman Chen Yuesheng reported on the new work remuneration standard regulations issued by Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press. The regulations stipulate the practice of calculating wages by day and by word for translation and compilation work, which not only disregards the personality of translators and compilers but also has a significant impact on the progress of Chinese culture. The colleagues have now publicly decided to fundamentally deny it and hope that all sectors will provide assistance. Next, Zhou Yutong explained the various malpractices of the standard regulations. Next, Wu Zhihui, a guest speaker, criticized the impropriety of paying by the word. Next, Pan Gongzhan, the director of the Social Bureau, reported on the mediation process. Next, Zhu Yinqing, Chen Tingrui, Hou Dachun, Xie Fusheng, and Kuang Fuzhuo, guests, spoke successively, all expressing dissatisfaction with the standard regulations and hoping that the Social Bureau would mediate properly so that the turmoil would not spread. Finally, the chairman expressed his thanks, and the meeting adjourned at 10:00 pm.

Shanghai's Little Luzon Aviation 99

Trial Flight on Thursday

Also Carrying Mail

The Phoenix biplane of Messageries Maritimes, located at No. 12 the Bund, was originally scheduled to fly to Little Luzon tomorrow morning at 8:00 am, piloted by Birofeu. However, due to the seven-hour flight over the sea between Shanghai and Little Luzon, and because the aircraft is a land-based aircraft, two 50-gallon fuel tanks must be added to carry extra gasoline for the sea flight and avoid the danger of landing halfway. The fuel tanks have not yet been completely installed. Therefore, the flight to Little Luzon has been changed to Thursday morning at 8:00 am, still departing from the Hongqiao Airport, first to Fuzhou overnight, then flying to Guangzhou the next day, and then flying to Little Luzon. Messageries Maritimes has also contacted the post office to have the aircraft carry mail. The postage from Shanghai to Little Luzon, in addition to the original 15 cents, will add an additional 15 cents for airmail.

Chuanhong Port Has Been Opened 101

Qidong County Government Informs Shanghai Shipping Company

The Shanghai Shipping Association notified the various shipping companies yesterday: "Greetings. According to Document No. 95 from the Qidong County Government, 'According to the report from Wu Feng, the technician of the Construction Shareholding Office of our county, since Chuanhong Port was silted up last year, Shanghai-Qidong ships have not been able to dock, which has caused considerable hardship for passengers. Now that the seawall and motor road have been completed one after another, and vehicles can travel directly to the outer port, the Shipping Association should be notified to inform the Shanghai-Qidong ships (1) Guangxiang ship of Dada Company, (2) Baofeng and Haimen ships of Jufeng Company, (3) Baohua ship of Ping'an Company, (4) Xinshengda ship of Xinlong Company, (5) Hongxing ship of Daxing Company, etc., to dock at Chuanhong Port on each voyage, in order to facilitate transportation and benefit travelers. This matter concerns the transportation of the entire county and should be submitted to your office for review and approval to notify the public, so that the public can benefit. Therefore, in addition to the instructions, we hereby request your association to investigate and handle the matter, and to inform the Shanghai-Qidong ships to dock at Chuanhong Port in order to facilitate transportation and benefit travelers. We sincerely hope to receive a reply. We hereby request that you investigate and handle the matter and look forward to receiving a reply.'"

Yangshupu Police Station Arrests Multiple Thieves 102

Yang A-quan of the Yangshupu Police Station, led several Western and Chinese detectives, armed, to a small teahouse at No. 132 Huishan Road at 2:00 pm the day before yesterday to arrest robbers. They arrested Li Jinxiang, a native of Jiangbei, who confessed that he was going to commit robbery somewhere and that his accomplices were waiting for him on Maohai Road. The Chinese and Western detectives then went to the location and arrested Jiang Jianchen and Hu Biku, two natives of Jiangbei. They then saw Jiang Wenli, a Jiangbei rickshaw puller, pulling an empty rickshaw and loitering in the area. A woman then came and hired Jiang's rickshaw, saying she was going to Yangshupu Bridge, but Jiang refused to go. The detectives noticed that Jiang was suspicious and searched him, finding a loaded pistol with six bullets in his chest. They took him and his rickshaw back to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Feng interrogated them. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that the defendants had committed several thefts since March of last year, and that the investigation was still ongoing. He requested an extension. Judge Feng then questioned the four defendants, Li, et al., and ordered them all to be detained for further investigation and trial.

Son Demands Money, Father Fires a Gun 103

Bullet Pierces Right Leg

Guan Siquan, a farmer from Zhenru Township in western Shanghai, is nearly seventy years old and makes a living by farming. He has two sons, A-da, 34 years old, and A-zhang, 31 years old, both of whom are married. They have separated from the family and started their own businesses. However, A-zhang is addicted to opium and does not work, so his life is very difficult. As the Lunar New Year is approaching, debts are being demanded, and his finances are tight. Last night, he asked his father for the land deed so that he could mortgage it to pay off his debts. His father refused, and they had an argument. His father became very angry and grabbed a gun from the security team and fired a shot, which hit A-zhang's right leg. The bullet pierced the leg, and the bone was broken. His wife accompanied him to Baolong Hospital for treatment.

Armed Robbery and Shooting in Hushu Li 104

Tao Haiyuan Cries for Help But Cannot Speak

Tao Haiyuan, a 64-year-old native of Nanhui, specializes in transporting cotton clothing. The cotton brought by the farmers from various villages in Pudong is all handled by Tao for sale to various cotton shops. He handles several thousand yuan in transactions every day. Tao has established an office at No. 15 Hushu Li, Limalu, Gongyi Wharf. Although Tao is over sixty, he is very diligent and thrifty and personally goes to the office every day to handle matters. His son, Tonghai, 38 years old, also assists his father in all matters at the office. Yesterday afternoon, at around 3:00 pm, Tao, his son, Tonghai, and a boatman, Tang Xuehai, were settling accounts at the office when three robbers suddenly appeared. They were all wearing long robes and speaking in a local accent. After entering the room, they all brandished handguns and drove Tao and the others to a corner, forbidding them to make any noise. One of the robbers immediately took the 2,300 yuan in cash and silver dollars on the account table (mostly Siming Bank notes) and put them in his pocket. Just as they were about to flee with the stolen goods, Tao Haiyuan realized that he was being robbed and shouted for help. But the words "save me" had just come out, and the word "life" had not yet been spoken. The merciless bullet had already been fired from the handgun held by one of the robbers, hitting Tao's left abdomen. He immediately fell to the ground, injured and bleeding. Seeing that they had caused a catastrophe, the robbers immediately rushed out the door, firing another shot at the house as they left. The bullet grazed Tang Xuehai, fortunately without causing any injury. At that time, the neighbors in the neighborhood suddenly heard the sound of gunfire and all opened their doors to look. They saw three men running out of house No. 15, saying that there was a fight inside and that there was nothing to see. They then left the alley and disappeared without a trace. Only after the neighbors entered house No. 15 did they realize that a huge sum of money had been robbed and that someone had been shot. Tao's son, Tonghai, and the boatman, Tang Xuehai, seeing that the robbers had gone far away, were slightly calmer. They found Tao Haiyuan lying on the ground, barely alive. They immediately took him to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. According to the hospital, the shot hit a vital organ and his life may be in danger.

Huang Lao San Cheats on His Friend's Wife 105

His Head Can Be Cut Off and Used as a Chamber Pot

Sun Dunwang, a 31-year-old native of Taizhou, lives on Suzhou Road in northern Shanghai and works as a shop assistant for a Japanese company. His wife, Chen, is not bad-looking and is the same age as Sun. Sun has a friend named Huang Lao San, who is now 31 years old. He often visits Sun's house, and Sun treats him kindly, allowing him to enter and leave the house freely without any restraint. Huang, however, is a beast in human clothing. He sees that Chen is beautiful and forgets Sun's friendship. He actually tries to seduce her. Over time, Chen falls under his spell, and they have an illicit affair. Because of Sun, they cannot do as they please. Therefore, on the 17th of this month, they eloped and hid in the Kade Road area in western Shanghai, planning to flee to the countryside. After his wife disappeared, Sun suspected that Huang had seduced her because no one else had visited his house. Therefore, at around 10:00 pm the day before yesterday, he went to Huang's place to inquire. Huang said, "You and I are close friends, how could I abduct your wife?" He then said, "If you find out that I abducted your wife in the future, you can cut off my head and use it as a chamber pot." Sun left after hearing this, but he still lurked nearby, watching his movements. Huang, seeing that Sun had left, knew that the news was tight. He quickly took Chen out of the house. Sun saw them by chance and followed them secretly. When they reached the Guan Bridge in Nanshi, they were about to board a ship. Sun immediately reported to the police of the Third Precinct, who came forward and arrested the man and woman and took them back to the First District Headquarters. After a preliminary hearing, they were ordered to be transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for investigation.

Huang Chujiu Passed Away Yesterday 106

Friends Organize a Funeral Committee

Mr. Huang Chujiu lived in Shanghai for forty years and engaged in various businesses, all of which were very successful. He was especially happy to donate to public welfare and charitable causes and was courageous in doing what was right. In the autumn and winter of last year, he suffered from severe asthma due to overwork, but he soon recovered. At the beginning of December, he went to Hangzhou to rest and stayed for more than a month. He returned to Shanghai from Hangzhou on January 2nd of this year. The fatigue in the car, coupled with more than a month of backlog of affairs in Shanghai, led to his diligent management and the recurrence of his old illness. He passed away at 4:10 pm yesterday (the 19th). The funeral will be held on the 21st (Wednesday). Mr. Huang founded many businesses during his lifetime. When he was ill, he left a will, entrusting his close friends to handle various funeral matters. After Mr. Huang passed away yesterday, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Yuan Ludeng, Ye Shantao, Huang Jinrong, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhao Qinbo, and others, held a meeting that night to organize a funeral committee. The members were generally appointed. Except for the Day and Night Bank and the sightseeing deposit department, which were temporarily entrusted to accountant Xu Yongzuo for sorting out, the rest remained the same. The detailed measures will be fully decided today. The following is a brief biography of Mr. Huang.

Mr. Huang Chujiu's Portrait

Mr. Huang, a native of Yuyao, Zhejiang, was originally named Chenggang, courtesy name Chujiu, later known by his courtesy name, and then changed his name to Cuojiu. He was a descendant of Mr. Lizhou, a great Confucian scholar of the late Ming Dynasty. His father, the elderly Zhiyi, was skilled in ophthalmology and was taught by an extraordinary person. He was especially known as a miracle worker. Mr. Huang followed his profession at a young age and read medical books extensively. He believed that Chinese medicine lacked the brain and organs, and the meaning was incomplete. Therefore, he resolutely gave up and devoted himself to the study of Western medicine. He founded the Zhongfa Pharmacy, and later also operated the Sino-Western Pharmacy. He also founded the Jiufu Company and issued dozens of beneficial medicines. In addition, he founded businesses such as the Great World, the Day and Night Bank, and the Fuchang Tobacco Company. There are countless other smaller ones. Mr. Huang also served as an executive member of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, chairman of the New Pharmaceutical Industry Association, a member of the West Lake Exposition Committee, and an economic member of the Red Cross Society. In the eighth year of the Republic, there was a major disaster in Henan, and people exchanged children for food. Mr. Huang sent people with funds to adopt more than a thousand infants. In the summer of the fifteenth year of the Republic, there was a major epidemic in Shanghai, and the dead were piled up. The existing epidemic hospital could not provide enough treatment. Mr. Huang resolutely initiated the epidemic hospital, which was completed in just ten days, saving many lives. He also independently built an ophthalmology hospital on Longmen Road, providing diagnosis and treatment at his own expense, without seeking donations. Mr. Huang's generosity is a model for the world.

However, the English-Chinese Automotive Terminology Record compiled will be published soon. Establishment of the China Cartoon News Agency 108

In recent years, the need for cartoons in Chinese publications has been increasing. However, there is still no suitable supply group. Now, the satirical cartoonist Mr. Huang Wennong, in view of the above-mentioned regret, resolutely founded the China Cartoon News Agency, gathering famous cartoonists to contribute their works to newspapers and magazines across the country as a war effort. Mr. Huang examined the situation in the international publishing industry and recognized that newspapers and magazines must use cartoons as a necessary condition to be successful publications of an era. The needs of readers of the era take cartoons as the driving force for promoting their thoughts. Because the power of cartoons lies in making up for the deficiencies of life and arousing the resonance of the public. Newspapers and magazines should publish cartoons based on the standpoint of freedom of speech in order to stimulate the spirit of the nation. Now, because Mr. Huang still has a part of his affairs that he cannot resign from, the agency is temporarily located at No. 2786 Anle Li, Zhoujiazui Road, this city. Send four cents in postage for the articles of association. The following is a warning within its articles of association: Newspapers and magazines that have a considerable history of publication and do not want to be outdated, please quickly add cartoons. Newspapers and magazines that are newly published and want to win a leading position in the public opinion, please quickly add cartoons. Newspapers and magazines are the mouthpiece of the people. If you want to achieve their true wishes, you must use cartoons. If you want to keep pace with the international publishing industry and win glory, you must use cartoons.

Letter to the Editor - To the Esteemed Editor, I am writing in response to a news item published on page 4 of your esteemed newspaper on the 17th regarding the China Merchants Inland Steam Navigation Bureau, which does not align with the facts and should be corrected to avoid misunderstandings. Since the Zhejiang Provincial Government took over this bureau in June of last year, and in order to unify accounting and supervise finances, the accounting director has been directly appointed by the provincial government, which has been very effective. The personnel dispatched only include two individuals from the Hangzhou General Bureau and the Shanghai Office, with a monthly salary of no more than one hundred yuan, which amounts to just over a thousand yuan annually. Furthermore, the business profit and loss rely on the enthusiasm of the managers and the planning to reform the long-standing malpractices.
