However, since this matter has been delayed for a long time, reorganizing the committee would further delay the matter. Therefore, the executive committee decided to conduct its own thorough and final review and, after careful study and consideration of all relevant facts, decided as follows: The players' departure for the competition without the prior consent of the Shanghai Western Soccer League was a violation of the league's regulations. However, the violation may have been due to unfamiliarity with the regulations rather than intentional disregard. The team manager, the liaison in Shanghai, and the representative in England were also in violation of these regulations. Furthermore, the players have undoubtedly violated the amateur sports rules of the English Football Association. However, the violation was likely due to unfamiliarity with the rules, and the team manager was also in violation of these rules. In view of this special situation, the council decided to issue a reprimand to all those involved in the team who are active in the various competitions under the protection of this council. If they wish to participate in the ball games hosted by the council in the future, they must abide by the regulations of the Shanghai Western Soccer League and the amateur sports rules of the English Football Association, otherwise, they will be permanently expelled from all amateur ball games related to this council. Feng Hao Sou and Frozen Tofu - Zheng Yimei - Since the beginning of the year, the weather has been freezing. Icicles hang from the eaves, reaching a foot in length. My family bought frozen tofu and cooked it with pork to accompany wine. It had a unique flavor. A guest who was acquainted with the late poet Feng Hao Sou said that Hao Sou loved to eat frozen tofu and drink wine to ward off the cold. He couldn't do without frozen tofu. He once composed a long poem about frozen tofu, but unfortunately, the manuscript was lost and never recovered. Otherwise, it could be passed down along with Yuan Mei's record of pig's head. In the summer, after eating plums and watermelon, he would definitely serve frozen tofu. But because it was hot, tofu couldn't be frozen, so he would store it in advance in the winter. The method was to take the frozen tofu and expose it to the sun. After it thawed into water and dried, the tofu became as hard as iron. Then, he would store it in a jar, sealing it tightly to prevent it from spoiling for a long time. In the summer, he would take it out of the jar and cook it, and it would be incomparably refreshing. Hao Sou would eat it with relish and it would improve his appetite. Hao Sou was good at calligraphy. He once said that there were six suitable conditions for practicing calligraphy: a clear breeze in the summer morning, a warm sun in the winter afternoon, after enjoying tea, after a light drink, a clever maid holding the inkstone, and a bright boy burning incense. Only a talented person could make such a wonderful statement. Hao Sou was fond of humor. He once had a long conversation with a guest. It was late in the year and the weather was cold. It looked like it would snow in the evening. Hao Sou invited the guest to drink at night. When they were drunk, Hao Sou said, "The ancients said that the three friends of winter are pine, bamboo, and plum. Then I have a long-standing relationship with the three friends." The guest asked him about it. He said, "Today, I'm using pine mushrooms and tofu to accompany bamboo leaf wine, and you are named Plum Creek. That is also the three friends." The guest smiled. They continued to drink. They didn't know that the snow outside the door was so deep that it had covered the horse's hooves. Wan Sou. Hao Sou was from Jintan. His name was Meng Hua. He had been a recluse in Shanghai for many years. He was one of the remnants of the past dynasty. Wind, Cold, and Moon Illuminate the Three Fragrant Graves - Ma Xiezong - Shanghai Cemetery is one of the four major cemeteries in Shanghai. It is located east of the Jiangwan Racecourse, in the Yin'hang Township. It is about seven or eight li from Jiangwan Town. The cemetery covers an area of about 200 mu and was founded by a wealthy merchant from Zhenhai. It was completed in the winter of the 17th year of the Republic (1928). This place is quiet and there are few cars. If the sun is shining and the wind is gentle, looking around makes one feel open-minded. However, on rainy days, wandering around can't help but bring a feeling of sadness. The cemetery is full of new tombs and steles, all of which have been built recently. In the western corner, there is the grave of Miss Shuxian, the daughter of Yu Youren, the director of the Control Yuan of the National Government. Slightly to the north, there is the grave of Miss Weiping, the daughter of Hu Pu'an, the director of the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department. Before their deaths, the two ladies once studied at the Chengdong Girls' School in Shanghai. Miss Yu was skilled in calligraphy, deeply rooted in family studies. Miss Hu was also skilled in calligraphy and painting. Her calligraphy was modeled after Zhao Huishu, and her paintings were copied from Huang Shiggu. After Miss Yu returned to Shaanxi with her father, the two were separated. From then on, they were at opposite ends of the earth, and their longing for each other increased. But human affairs are impermanent, and ephemeral mushrooms wither easily. Therefore, in less than a few years, the two ladies passed away one after another, which is very sad. Now, the two ladies are buried in the same cemetery, with their fragrant graves next to each other. It may not be a coincidence. If they knew in the afterlife, their friendship would be even greater than when they were alive. And in the wind and rain, at dawn and dusk, their souls would have companions, so they would not be lonely and miserable. Also in the cemetery, there is another tomb, with the inscription "Grave of Beloved Daughters Nana and Tingting". The names are very beautiful. It is unknown whose daughters are buried here. After paying respects, it is even more sad. Cheng Zai Yanqiu's Prayer for Peace Is Careful - Cheng Yanqiu's newly written play "Tears on the Barren Mountain," also called "Prayer for Peace," has been completed. The description is as follows: This play is based on a story from the Ming Dynasty. It tells the story of Gao Liangmin, a hunter in Jiyuan County, his wife Chen, his son Zhong, his daughter-in-law Zhang Huizhu, and his grandson Baolian. Although their circumstances are poor, their family is harmonious and they enjoy the joys of family life. Because Yang Sichang believed that the military expenses were insufficient, he advocated the levy of military rations and training rations, and then requested an increase in taxes. At that time, the yamen runners ran rampant, and the people complained. Gao Liangmin and his son were trapped in paying taxes. They struggled to hunt, but both were killed by tigers. His grandson Baolian was captured by the government army and became a soldier. Chen was so grieved that she vomited blood and died. The only one left was Zhang Huizhu, who was alone and miserable. The plot is very simple, but the details are carefully crafted. Cheng Yanqiu plays Zhang Huizhu. At first, she used her hard-earned weaving to pay taxes, but then she suffered repeated family tragedies and had to support herself alone. Finally, she was forced by evil runners and had no way out. She lamented that she had suffered from war and chaos. She lamented her life and sympathized with the people. So, she fled to the barren valley and cried out to heaven. She expressed her deep compassion and prayed for peace. She was willing to die for the people. This is the focus of the entire play. In the scene of waiting for her husband on a moonlit night, she sings "Nanbangzi". Her surprise, suspicion, and fear become more and more intense. In the scene of seeing her husband in the air, she sings "Kuaiban". Her resentment and madness are like being drunk. She portrays the situation vividly and realistically. In the final scene, she uses "Yaoban" to make a desolate cry. The world is old and the sky is barren, and her blood is dry and her tears are exhausted. Viewers at this point cannot help but feel sad and shed tears of sympathy to call for peace. Over Two Hundred Fishing Boats Burned by Pirates 111

Naval Gunboats Head to Suppress

Recently, outside of Wu Song Port and along the coastal areas of various counties such as Tongzhou, Rugao, Hai'an, and Qidong, large groups of pirate ships, numbering over a hundred, have reappeared, traveling to and from the sea and various ports, burning and looting extensively with extreme ferocity. The fishing boats along the coast, as the autumn fishing season has ended, are currently gathered in ports along the coast to rest for the winter, engaged in repairing nets in preparation for setting sail in the spring. They have all been surrounded by pirate ships, which coerce the fishing households to pay protection money, ranging from fifty to five hundred yuan depending on the size of the fishing boat, divided into ten grades. (It is said that after the fishing boats pay the money to the pirates, the pirates give them a yellow flag with the pirate's seal on it as a mark. Afterwards, when the fishing boats set sail, they raise the yellow flag on the ship's mast, and the pirates will not rob them, beautifully calling it protection money.) If the fishing boats do not comply, they are set on fire by the pirates. As a result, according to the survey results, over two hundred fishing boats have been burned by pirates in recent days. Those that have not been reported are not included. The fishing boats are quite panicked. Xu Mianqin, the captain of the 17th squad of the 4th district of the Wu Song Naval Police, and Lin Junsheng, the captain of the 18th squad, after receiving the report the day before yesterday, have already led the Hai Ping, Yang Duan, Hai Deng gunboats and two squads of patrol boats to sail to the coastal area to suppress them.

Xu Lichih Invents Locust-Exterminating Paste 112

The loss to our country's agricultural production due to locust plagues amounts to hundreds of millions every year. However, the methods of controlling locusts still follow the old methods of driving, capturing, and burying, etc. There has never been a fundamental extermination using scientific methods with medicine. Xu Lichih of Beiping, who has long been dedicated to horticulture, invented a locust-exterminating paste last year, made entirely from domestic raw materials. One tael of the paste can be mixed with water at a ratio of 800 to 1200 times. After mixing with water, it is sprayed into the fields with a sprayer. Areas already afflicted with locusts can be instantly paralyzed, or they will smell the scent and fly away, not daring to land. The paste not only exterminates locusts, but also drives away all pests that harm crops, without harming crops, livestock, or humans. Its value is extremely low, and its protection is extremely high. In the future, after it is launched, it will greatly benefit the agricultural and horticultural communities. He is currently applying to the Ministry of Industry for registration and patent, and ordering all provincial agricultural departments to instruct rural villages to purchase it. He also intends to seek cooperation from domestic capitalists to establish a large-scale factory to manufacture and launch it.

100,000 Yuan Smuggled Aboard New Beijing Steamer Last Night 113

Shanghai Banks Transport Funds to Ningbo for Profit

Detention, Assessment of Fines to be Discussed

Recently, Ningbo has been lacking in cash, and silver dollars have soared in value. Banks in this city are transporting cash to Ningbo to profit from this. Yesterday, someone attempted to smuggle a large sum of money, hoping to evade taxes. Customs officers discovered 100,000 yuan on the New Beijing steamer and immediately requested a fine. The following is a report of what was heard.

One Hundred Thousand Yuan Secretly Transported Recently, cash in the Ningbo market has been extremely tight, and exchange rates have skyrocketed. Bank staff see this as a great source of profit and are collecting cash to send to Ningbo. In a single transfer, they can earn huge profits. This cash is transported to Ningbo by sea, which is a short distance, requiring only one night. Therefore, they often entrust it to steamer crew members, giving them a small reward to avoid the hassle of customs declarations and evade customs duties. Yesterday, a certain bank, etc., divided 100,000 national currency into twenty boxes to be transported to Ningbo. They had contacted the crew of the Taikoo New Beijing steamer in advance and secretly loaded it into the ship to be unloaded in Ningbo. It was already loaded by 5:00 PM, and after the passengers were all on board, the ship set sail.

Discovered by Customs Officers The Customs Patrol Department, which inspects ships departing the port, must check for contraband and smuggled goods. The customs officers searched the forward hold crew quarters and discovered a large amount of cash that had not been declared, clearly indicating that it was being smuggled. They immediately notified the ship's captain to temporarily delay the ship's departure and reported it to the customs office, who detained the cash.

Sending a Steamer to Extract the Cash The Jianghai Customs received the report and immediately dispatched a small steamer to the Taikoo Wharf. Under the supervision of the customs officers, the 100,000 yuan was removed from the crew quarters and loaded onto the small steamer, which transported it back to the customs warehouse for safekeeping, pending investigation of the banks involved and assessment of fines according to smuggling regulations. The cash was not completely unloaded and removed until 7:00 PM. The New Beijing Delayed Departure The New Beijing steamer was originally scheduled to depart at 5:00 PM. However, due to the cash being discovered by customs and the subsequent unloading and removal, it was unable to depart on time. It did not leave port until 7:30 PM, over two hours later than the original scheduled departure time.

The Truth About the Suicide of Yih Ho Employee Shen Shou Kang 114

Due to Gambling Addiction and Embezzlement of Public Funds

This newspaper reported on the 16th that Shen Shou Kang, a clerk in the accounting department of Yih Ho Foreign Firm, had committed suicide by drowning. According to another source, Shen had worked in the Yih Ho accounting department for five or six years, earning a monthly salary and an annual bonus, totaling around one hundred yuan per month. Initially, he was quite frugal. However, recently, due to a gambling addiction, he repeatedly misappropriated public funds. His father had helped him make up for it twice. This time, he had embezzled over three thousand yuan, which he could not account for, and used fake receipts to cover it up. His superior colleague, Mr. Zhang, discovered this and urged him to repay the money quickly, otherwise, if the compradore found out, it would be difficult to remedy. Shen then excused himself to go out and raise funds, but never returned. He sent a suicide note to his colleagues, saying that he had decided to jump into the sea to die. His whereabouts are still unknown. It is not yet known whether he is truly dead. His father pleaded with the compradore's office to compensate for the embezzlement and said that such an unfilial son had lost his life due to gambling, and even his death was not to be regretted.

Communist Bandits from Taixing Arrested in Shanghai 115

Last year, in August and September, Taixing County in Jiangbei was repeatedly ravaged by communist bandits. Cases of arson, murder, and kidnapping occurred frequently. Although the military and police pursued and suppressed them, the major criminals all escaped the net. Huang Zhengxuan, the captain of the 4th squad of the 2nd district of the Taixing County Defense Corps, recently received a secret report that the bandit leader Ye Hongbin (also known as Wang Boxun) of Taixing had fled to Shanghai and was hiding at 54 Wenzhou Road. He specifically requested the county government to prepare a document, and Captain Huang personally came to Shanghai. The day before yesterday, he, together with detectives from the New Zha Police Station, secretly went to the address to arrest him. They arrested Ye and his accomplice Xiao Ruihong (also known as Zhu Guozhai). Yesterday, they were taken to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Ge interrogated them. According to Wang Yaotang, the lawyer of the police station, the document from Taixing only mentioned Ye and not Xiao Ruihong. He requested that Xiao be temporarily detained in the police station until the document for his transfer arrived. When questioned, Ye confessed that his hometown had been ravaged by communist bandits last year. The bandits wanted to coerce him, but he was unwilling to become a bandit, so his house was burned down. He then fled to Shanghai and had not committed any crimes. Xiao Ruihong confessed that he used to work in a factory in Wuxi and had come to Shanghai the day before yesterday, staying at Ye's place, and knew nothing else. Judge Ge concluded the preliminary hearing and ordered Ye Hongbin to be taken away by Captain Huang for handling according to the law. Xiao Ruihong was temporarily detained in the police station, and the county government should prepare a letter, detailing the facts of the crime, and send it to the court for review.
